Strict Prohibition of Porters' Extortion on the Beijing-Shanghai Railway 95

The porters at various stations on the Beijing-Shanghai Railway are supposed to charge eight copper coins per piece for carrying passengers' luggage. However, the porters have recently been disobeying the regulations and extorting at will, even demanding as much as one small ocean (silver dollar) per piece. Passengers are suffering from this. The Beijing-Shanghai Railway Bureau, in view of this, and in order to protect the interests of passengers, has issued a special order to station inspectors. If any porter dares to extort in violation of the regulations, they should report it to the Traffic Department for severe punishment.

Shanghai South Public Bus

Route 3 Loop Line Information 96

The Shanghai South Public Bus Route 3 originally ran between Laoximen and Gaochangmiao. Later, due to poor business, it was changed to run on Zhonghua Road. Later, in order to facilitate passengers traveling north, it continued to run on Minguo Road, forming a Route 3 loop line. The section of the route belonging to the urban area was opened to traffic on November 6, 1929. The section in the French Concession, because it belongs to the business scope of the French Tram and Electric Light Company, must first be discussed and agreed upon with the French company. The Shanghai South Public Bus Company has already negotiated a contract with the French company and submitted it to the Public Utilities Bureau for transfer to the Municipal Government for approval. It is expected that it will be put into operation soon.

Zhou Tingyi Commits Suicide by Poison 99

With Four Suicide Notes

Zhou Tingyi, a 23-year-old from Wuxi, worked as a waiter at the Cathay Hotel on Nanjing Road. He took leave to return to his hometown on the 10th of this month. He returned to Shanghai a week later and spent the night at the Sanjiang Hostel on Beihai Road on the evening of the 18th, arriving at midnight. The next morning, the room service attendant knocked on Zhou's room, No. 30, but there was no response. Suspecting something was wrong, he opened the door and saw the guest lying stiffly on the bed. He was rushed to the hospital. After examination, it was found that he had taken opium. When trying to resuscitate him, he had lost his mind and refused to take medicine. He soon died. Afterward, four suicide notes were found in the hostel, addressed to his grandmother and mother-in-law. Reading between the lines, it seemed that he was in debt and could not make up for the losses, and he resorted to this desperate measure. There was still residual pain in the words. The deceased married last winter. His wife's name was Yueqin. There were no children.

Wife Gone and Not Returning 100

Clothes and Jewelry Vanished

Husband Files for Divorce

Chen Deyi, the twenty-five-year-old owner of a rice shop in Yangsi Township, Pudong, lost his wife, Cai, to illness in 1925. Subsequently, through the matchmaking of Li Amao and a Mr. Zhou, he remarried a Miss Gong from Sanlin Township, the daughter of Gong Yutang. They were married on the third day of the second month of the fifteenth year of the Republic. Unexpectedly, after Miss Gong entered the household, she frequently used excuses to return to her parents' home, staying for several days before returning. Chen often went to his in-laws' home to pick her up, only to find she had disappeared, causing him considerable suspicion. On the tenth day of the first month of the lunar calendar last year, Miss Gong again used an excuse to return to her parents' home and never came back, despite repeated attempts to contact her. Chen then checked his wife's clothing and jewelry, only to find they had all vanished. He went to his in-laws' home to question them, but Miss Gong refused to see him. Unable to endure this any longer, Chen retained lawyer Qu Yue to file a petition for divorce with the local court. The case was heard in the seventh courtroom by Judge Zhang Jinjian on the afternoon of the day before yesterday at 2 p.m. The plaintiff, along with his lawyer and witnesses, appeared in court. The defendant, Chen Gong, did not appear. After the judge took his seat, the plaintiff, Chen Deyi, recounted the previous events, stating that the clothes of his deceased wife, Cai, in the chest had all been damaged by the defendant, Chen Gong, who had broken the chest's hinges and taken away more than twelve items of clothing. (Question) When were you married? (Answer) The third day of the second month of the fifteenth year of the Republic. (Question) Was your marriage good? (Answer) Initially, it was harmonious, but in June of that year, according to local custom, the new bride had to return to her mother's home for a summer rest. She returned home as usual, for about a week. The plaintiff went to pick her up, but the defendant was not at home. According to his mother-in-law, she had gone to Shanghai. The plaintiff had no choice but to return disappointed. Two days later, the defendant was sent back by her father, Gong Yutang. (Question) What does Gong Yutang do for a living? (Answer) Gong is a clerk at Hengfeng Rice Shop at Wanyu Wharf. At the time, I asked my father-in-law what the defendant was doing in Shanghai. My father-in-law said he did not know. My father-in-law then scolded the defendant, but the defendant was very unrestrained and showed irregular behavior. The plaintiff has unspeakable reasons, and so on. Next, the witness Cai Changsheng testified, age fifty-three, local resident, living in Bailianjing. Chen Deyi is my son-in-law. My daughter died of illness on the twenty-ninth day of the fifth month of the fourteenth year of the Republic. The following year, my son-in-law remarried Miss Gong. (Question) Was their marriage good? (Answer) Initially, it was good, but later, because Miss Gong had improper behavior, it was no longer good. In November of the year before last (1928), one day, just before dawn, Miss Gong suddenly came to my house. I knew that Miss Gong did not live at her mother's home, because my son-in-law had told me the day before. At the time, I asked her to eat breakfast. After breakfast, I planned to send her to my son-in-law's house, but I met Gong Yutang on the way. So Gong accompanied his daughter to her husband's house. (Question) How many clothes did your daughter have when she got married? (Answer) More than one hundred pieces. (Question) Were many pieces taken by Miss Gong? (Answer) Miss Gong definitely took them away successively, and so on. At this point in the questioning, the plaintiff's lawyer stated, although the witness Cai Changsheng is the father-in-law of the plaintiff, his daughter is deceased and he is now a kind of relative. This testimony should be adopted. The judge announced that the defendant was not present today and the hearing would be continued at a later date. The court was then adjourned.

Divorce with Conditions 101

Judge Mediates in Court

Zhu Xingbao, a young woman from this city, recently retained lawyer Xu Xingti to sue her husband, Yu Afu, in the local court for abuse, abandonment, and failure to provide support, requesting a divorce. The court had previously held a hearing on the case, but it was not concluded. Yesterday morning, Judge Yang Keqian held another hearing. After briefly questioning both parties, the judge attempted to mediate a settlement in court. Initially, neither party would comply, but after an hour of the judge's persuasion, a settlement was reached. The plaintiff, Zhu Xingbao, paid the defendant, Yu Afu, two hundred yuan. The defendant then returned a suitcase and twelve items of clothing to the plaintiff. Both parties expressed satisfaction. After the judge gave some further guidance to both parties, the judge drafted a settlement record in court and ordered both parties to sign it. From then on, they separated like scattered swallows, severing all ties. The court was then adjourned.

A Group Forcibly Abducts a Woman 102

Rickshaw Driver Thinks It's Kidnapping

Actually an Attempt at Extortion

Zhang Sibao, a woman from Changzhou, just turned twenty. She came to Shanghai with her husband in the spring of 1928 and found work in a yarn factory through an acquaintance. Before long, her husband was idle and unemployed, and life was difficult. He pawned Sibao into the Wu surname brothel in the Xiaohua Garden in the Public Concession, for a term of two years. Sibao entered a cage, as this flesh and blood career was compelled to be like this, and it was something she was not really willing to do. Time passed quickly, and now the term has expired, and her husband is nowhere to be found. She wants to leave the sea of suffering, but she has nowhere to live. Recently, there was a customer named Xia Jinbao, who was very like-minded with her. Sibao then left the Wu surname brothel last week and went straight to Xia Jinbao's home at No. 8 Xie Xingli, Bailinan Road, Western Shanghai. Xia has not yet married, and he is happy to have such a good partner, so they are together. Unexpectedly, good things are often hampered. Suddenly, three or four of Xia's fellow offenders, Wang Qiaolin and Zhu Xiaoliu, thought they were having fun together, and their jealousy flared up and tried to stop them in every possible way. Seeing that Sibao was determined, they decided to collude to extort money. The night before last, they went to Xia's house to extort forty yuan from Xia. Xia refused to pay because he had no money to raise. Yesterday afternoon, at about 4 p.m., Wang, Zhu, and the other three or four men waited near Xia's residence. Soon Sibao went out to shop. Wang and the others rushed up and grabbed Sibao. At the same time, they hired a taxi with the Concession registration number 17767 and dragged Sibao into the car, intending to take her to the Concession and find a way to deal with her. Unexpectedly, the driver saw a group of people forcibly abducting a woman and was afraid of being kidnapped. He was suspicious and frightened, so he stopped the car at the intersection of Yidingpan Road after only a few steps. He was about to report to the police there, but Wang and the others saw the opportunity and panicked, jumping out and fleeing. Only the woman was left in the car. The driver immediately turned around and drove back to the Wujiaochang area of Bailinan Road, immediately reported to the patrol chief of the sixth district, and took the woman back to the sixth district police station to await investigation.

Gao Mingsheng Inappropriately Gropes Breast 103

Zhu Huang, a twenty-two-year-old woman from Changzhou, residing in Maojia Lane outside the Dadongmen, is still pretty. At about 3 p.m. yesterday afternoon, she went to Beishi to shop. When she was walking to the Guomalu intersection of the 16th Pier, Gao Mingsheng, a Tongzhou man who works as a boatman, came up to her in a hurry. He raised his hands and touched her chest, groping her breasts, and then ran away immediately. She quickly chased after him and managed to grab him. She then called out to Zang Yaochen, the guard at the twelfth post there, who took him back to the First District Headquarters. He was ordered to be detained temporarily, pending preliminary review by the District Chief.

Lawyers Association Asks for Punishment of Ding Lei 109

The Standing Committee of the Lawyers Association sent a telegram to the military and judicial organs in Beijing and Jiangsu, saying: To President Wang of the Nanjing Judicial Yuan, Minister Zhu of the Ministry of Justice, President Lin of the Supreme Court, Chief Prosecutor of the Procuratorate, Minister of Military and Political Affairs, President Lin of the Jiangsu High Court in Suzhou, and Chief Prosecutor Wang, I admire your deeds. Recently, our members Cai Nipei, Shan Yuhua, Shen Zhaojiu, and Liu Zuwang sent letters stating that Ding Lei, the warden of the Third Branch Prison of Jiangsu and the director of the detention center, transferred dozens of criminal defendants from the prison to the Second Army Prison, where they were treated as convicted military prisoners. The families of the parties concerned have repeatedly requested guarantees. In addition to the victims filing a lawsuit against the director of the prison according to the law, please send a telegram to the competent authority according to the situation, quickly suspend the director of the prison from his post and bring him to justice for interrogation, and at the same time transfer all the offenders who were sent to the Army Prison back to protect them. It is said that the regulations of the detention center have clear provisions on the extent of the restrictions on the food, clothing, housing, and transportation of criminal defendants in custody, while the treatment in prisons is even more severe. They shall not be sent to prison for execution until the verdict is final and guilty. The Army Prison is not within the scope of the judiciary, and its treatment is even more different from that of ordinary prisons. The director of the prison transferred criminal defendants who had not been convicted to the Army Prison, which is obviously an abuse of power. Moreover, the Army Prison, regardless of the crime of each prisoner or whether there is a legal certificate from the superior officer, will accept them, which not only tramples on human rights and destroys the dignity of the judiciary, but also has this shocking act at the time of the abolition of consular jurisdiction, which is enough to make people laugh at home and abroad and obstruct the recovery of legal rights. For this reason, we respectfully request your attention, and order the director of the prison, Ding Lei, to be suspended from his post and brought to justice for interrogation, and immediately transfer the offenders in the Army Prison to ensure that the truth is corrected and to maintain the dignity of the judiciary. Liu Zuwang, Jiang Yiping, and Yu Zhongluo, standing committee members of the Shanghai Lawyers Association, kowtow.

Display Methods of National Products Department Stores 110

Rules for Displaying Samples

The China National Products Department Store has specially set up a display department to solicit displays of domestic products in order to facilitate various manufacturers and promote their products. The rules for displaying samples are recorded as follows: This department store is specially set up with a display department to promote national products for the public to view in accordance with the organizational outline. All manufacturers who wish to send their goods or samples, specimens, models, etc. to this department store for display shall pay a fee of three yuan per square zhang per day, which shall be charged according to the size of the area occupied, excluding the designated public passages. The fee shall be calculated per square foot per day. The display counters required by each manufacturer shall be prepared by the exhibitor himself, but they must conform to the standard style stipulated by this department store. If there are particularly beautiful counters, their drawings must be submitted to the director of the field affairs section for approval in advance. The decorations required shall be prepared by the exhibitor himself. All manufacturers who send products for display and pay the location fee calculated per square foot per day will not be charged a separate publicity fee by this department store to show preferential treatment. The displayed items shall be managed by personnel dispatched by this department store. Exhibitors are welcome to dispatch their own personnel to keep or explain them. However, the displayed machines must be wiped by machine workers specially dispatched by the exhibitor on a regular basis to prevent rust damage. Manufacturers who send products for display must fill in an exhibition application form, together with the displayed products, and send them to the receiving and dispatching office of this department store for a receipt, and then the receiving and dispatching office will transfer them to the display department for display. This department store shall be fully responsible for the safekeeping of the displayed items sent to this department store, except for those that are beyond human power. However, the exhibitor shall be responsible for the safety and fire insurance. When exhibitors who send products for display return their products, they must submit the receipt issued by this department store. If the receipt is lost, they must invite a reliable shop as a guarantor or publish a statement in the newspaper before this department store can return the products. If there are any inadequacies in these rules, the display department may submit them to the manager of this department store for revision.

Assisting in the Implementation of Stamp Duty 112

Shops That Do Not Affix Stamps Will Be Sued

Since the Jiangsu Stamp Duty Office in Shanghai appointed Liu Chunpu and Shen Rulin as special commissioners for stamp duty in the French Concession, the French Concession Stamp Duty Office has made active progress on stamp duty in the French Concession for two months, and the results have been improving day by day. Now that the shops in the Public Concession that do not affix stamps have been negotiated by the Shanghai Stamp Duty Office to be sued by the police to the Special Court for fines at any time, the two special commissioners Liu and Shen specially requested the Jiangsu Stamp Duty Office in Shanghai to formally contact the French Concession authorities and planned to follow the example of the Public Concession. It is now known that the two special commissioners Liu and Shen have received a reply from the Shanghai Office and have negotiated with the French authorities. All shops in the French Concession that have not affixed stamps will immediately implement a search for evidence and select those who are punished. The original letter is recorded below: To start with, regarding the punishment of the shops in the French Concession that have not affixed stamps, this office has negotiated with the French Concession authorities. Now it is urgent to select those who are punished to serve as a warning. Please check more than ten or even twenty documents (one for each family) and send them to this office for verification and handling, and I hope to do so as soon as possible.

In addition, the French Concession Stamp Duty Office issued a notice to various shops, saying: For the matter of notification, it is found that these special commissioners have been appointed by the Shanghai Office of the Stamp Duty Bureau of Jiangsu Province of the Ministry of Finance to handle stamp duty matters in the French Concession, and they have rented No. 18 Zhenpingli, Gelo Road, and started work on April 1. It has been notified repeatedly, and the General Assembly of Representatives of the Taxpaying Chinese in the French Concession and the Road Chambers of Commerce has also been notified in a comprehensive manner. Stamp duty is a good tax that is commonly used in various countries, and it is collected from merchants and the people. The amount is very small. Affixing stamps only costs one or two cents. Once something happens, it can have the effect of proving legal benefits. The national tax revenue relies on this to accumulate small amounts into large amounts. The merchants and people in the concession are all members of the national community. They should all inspire patriotism and use stamps together. It has been decided that the Public Concession will implement inspections this month, and those who hide and do not affix stamps will be sued for punishment. The French Concession is the same. The authorities have been asked to investigate and handle it. If the merchants in the concession rely on their establishment in the concession and make excuses to wait and see and try to be opportunistic, once they are found out, they will be reported to the police and asked to be summoned to the French public office on a household basis and punished according to the law. The special commissioners will take measures to seek peace. The merchants in the concession should all follow this intention and not lose sight of the bigger picture and hurt their reputation. For this reason, this notice is issued, and all merchants and people should abide by it. They must all check themselves, and those who have missed it should affix the stamps as soon as possible. Once they are found out and reported, it will be too late to regret it. Do not misunderstand yourselves.

Ministry of Finance Approves Rectification of Anti-Smuggling Measures 116

Instruct the Anti-Smuggling Agencies to Comply

The Ministry of Finance previously received a report from the Anti-Smuggling Department of the Salt Affairs Inspection General Office on seven anti-smuggling rectification measures, which were considered pertinent and specially approved. The Salt Transport Envoys and Anti-Smuggling Agencies were ordered to handle them. The Anti-Smuggling Bureau of the five Jiangsu properties in this city received the instruction yesterday, saying: In order to carry out the order, according to the Anti-Smuggling Department of the Salt Affairs Inspection General Office, I secretly investigated that salt affairs anti-smuggling matters and the inspection and tax collection have a close relationship. If we do not cooperate fully, it is difficult to achieve good results. Now that the Anti-Smuggling Department has been established recently, it is time for the two parties to cooperate. With the consent of both parties after consultation, it is planned to appoint the responsible personnel of the inspection departments in each property, the assistant inspection officers and the assistant staff directly under the jurisdiction of the Inspection General Office as anti-smuggling supervisors in each property. Several articles of the regulations for the supervisors' offices are also proposed as follows: (1) All responsible personnel of the inspection departments shall be appointed by the Ministry to concurrently serve as anti-smuggling officer supervisors in the tax collection area under their jurisdiction. (2) If the anti-smuggling supervisor finds that any anti-smuggling officer, soldier, or soldier violates the regulations or the orders of the anti-smuggling department, or proves that there is a corrupt act, and there is definite evidence, he may notify the director of the anti-smuggling bureau to handle it, or report it to the inspection general office so that it can be transferred to the anti-smuggling department for verification and handling. (3) If the anti-smuggling supervisor has any suggestions for improving anti-smuggling matters, he shall consult with the director of the anti-smuggling bureau, and may report it to the inspection general office for transfer to the anti-smuggling department for verification and handling. (4) If the anti-smuggling bureau dismisses personnel without the order of the anti-smuggling department or without sufficient reason, and appoints people locally to supplement them, the anti-smuggling supervisor shall report it to the inspection general office for transfer to the anti-smuggling department for verification and handling. (5) If the director of the anti-smuggling bureau has any situation to report to the anti-smuggling department regarding the appointment or dismissal of personnel, he shall send a letter to the anti-smuggling supervisor for verification so that he can express his opinions on the situation to the inspection general office for reference and verification by the anti-smuggling department. (6) All administrative matters within the authority of the director of the anti-smuggling bureau and the official correspondence between the anti-smuggling department shall be conveyed by the inspection general office. If the above-mentioned regulations are approved, the officials shall notify the various districts to check and implement them. Whether the proposed anti-smuggling measures are appropriate, the principles are reported for verification, etc. It should be approved. Yesterday, the ministry ordered the responsible personnel of the inspection agencies in each district to concurrently serve as anti-smuggling supervisors in each district, and notified them separately. The bureau was ordered to know this order, etc.

Over seven hundred workers in the mechanical department of the French Water and Electricity Company, due to unmet demands, initiated a slowdown strike. It has been three days. The declaration and advisory letter are recorded below.

Declaration of the French Water and Electricity Workers' Union on being forced to strike: We, the seven hundred workers, have been rejected and not accepted by the capitalist French Water and Electricity Company. They have locked their iron gates and driven us seven hundred workers out, without even listening to us. What a heartbreaking matter! We workers spend the whole day working like machines for the capitalists, and the wages we earn with our sweat are not enough to buy food. This is not how things should be under the leadership of the Three Principles of the People. The wage increase we workers are requesting this time is very limited. Other demands, such as an eight-hour workday and year-end bonuses, are not excessive. However, the capitalists, with a bit of conscience, should have been able to sympathize with our cries of suffering and misery from exhaustion. But their exploitative and oppressive measures are commonplace and not surprising at all. Our appeals are like idle dreams. Therefore, three notices were met with stern rejection and extreme rigidity, which aroused the anger of the workers. A meeting resolved to unanimously start a slowdown strike on the 18th to awaken the factory. Unexpectedly, instead of us slowing down, they simply wanted us to start a strike. On the morning of the 19th, our workers went to the factory as usual to slow down, but the factory actually drove the workers out and closed the iron gates. Alas, this rigid attitude has made us disappointed and saddened. We now really want to strike but cannot. Our strike can be completely attributed to the factory's creation and oppression. We now only request assistance from higher party and government agencies on the one hand, and on the other hand, we all unite together, vow to persevere to the end, and strive peacefully. We will never give up until we achieve our goals. Our slogans: (1) Workers unite together! (2) Implement the Three Principles of the People! (3) Realize the Three-Eight System! (4) Overthrow the running dogs colluding with capital! (5) Strictly prevent reactionary elements from taking advantage of the situation! (6) Support the French Water and Electricity Workers' Union!

Advisory Letter from the Workers' Union to Chinese Staff of the Company requesting assistance: Dear Sirs, The reason our union members are making demands to the capitalists this time is a matter of vital importance to our livelihoods. Unexpectedly, the capitalists sternly rejected us with three notices. The Municipal Party Department and the Social Bureau have mediated, but the capitalists' attitude is rigid, which is truly unbearable. Furthermore, they closed the iron gates yesterday morning and deceived and drove away the workers, causing hundreds of workers to want to strike but be unable to. The capitalists' oppression of us Chinese workers could not be worse. Moreover, any of our compatriots with a little conscience cannot but be filled with indignation. Our union, on behalf of all workers, vows to fight to the death and will not stop until we achieve our goals. Correspondingly, we respectfully request you to investigate. We hope that comrades will uphold the spirit of mutual assistance among compatriots, rise up and shout, and assist the workers. We will be eternally grateful.

Aberrations of Family Economic Oppression 121

Shi Guanlin Couple Quarrel

Shi Guanlin, a Jin Tan native residing at No. 187 Tangjia Lane, works as a helmsman on inland riverboats. His wife, Zhou, works at a nearby silkworm moth (also known as scraps) factory. They have four children. Guanlin has been ill for a long time and has been sitting at home eating away at their resources. Recently, due to the large population, they often suffer from food shortages. He gave his eight-year-old son to a friend to ease the burden. Zhou did not want this, and quarrels often arose. In his resentment and anger, Guanlin suddenly had a pessimistic thought of ending his life. Yesterday afternoon, while his wife went to work at the factory, he swallowed opium in an attempt to die. When Zhou returned home from work, she saw her husband lying stiff on the bed, unresponsive, with a pale face. She found the remaining opium on the ground. Realizing he had taken poison, she immediately rushed him to Puji Hospital. According to the doctor, he must vomit out the poison, otherwise his life would be in danger.

Female Hostess Requests Divorce 123

Unsuccessful Mediation in Court

Judgment Scheduled for the 26th

Huang Niu (i.e. Huang Qihong), a Cantonese man, works in the shipping industry. His wife, Deng Fengjin, is also from Guangdong. The couple is the same age, 32 years old each. Deng is quite independent and currently works as a hostess at a merchant club in the French Concession. Her income is not bad and she does not need to rely on her husband for a living. Therefore, she filed for divorce at the Special District Local Court. Yesterday morning, Judge Xu Wenrong held a court hearing. According to the plaintiff Deng Fengjin, she married Huang on April 14th, 1911. They were initially in love, but after Huang lost his job, he became addicted to gambling and smoking. His family had no permanent property, so I had to throw myself into a merchant club in the French Concession as a hostess to make a living. Later, Huang also found a job on a Wuhu ship, but he still did not send any money home. Although I had a slight wage, it was not enough to cover expenses, so I borrowed money to get by. I now owe no less than a thousand yuan. Four years ago, Huang returned to Shanghai from Wuhu and asked me for a hundred yuan. I gave him seventy yuan, and since then he has been asking me for forty-five yuan per month, otherwise he would threaten me. On the 18th of last month, he again forcibly demanded money. I had no choice but to take my six-year-old adopted daughter and temporarily return to my mother's home to avoid his demands. Since he does not support me, I request a divorce. Huang Niu testified that he married Deng in the Republic of China in 1909. Since I found a job on a ship, I have never asked Deng for a cent. But because she worked at the club, I was indeed dissatisfied, but she would not listen. I told her father, but he could not control her either, saying she was free to do as she pleased. She became more reckless, and her romantic behavior spread among the public. A certain tabloid once recorded it. To save face, I decided to take her to live in Wuhu and ordered her to resign from her hostess job, but she did not take my words seriously and neither resigned nor left. She still holds the position, staying out all night and returning only at dawn. I am not wealthy, and marrying one wife is already extremely difficult. I cannot agree to the plaintiff's request for divorce. Her so-called debt of more than a thousand yuan was also spent by herself, and I never received a penny from it. He also hired a lawyer to argue that the plaintiff's request for divorce was for other purposes, which would be realized after the divorce. The lawyers from both sides argued with each other, and Judge Xu advised the plaintiff to take a step back and reconcile. However, she insisted on her position, so the court did not waste any more words and ordered the parties to wait for the verdict on the morning of the 26th of this month.

Continuing to Arrest Accomplices in the Pudong Robbery Case 124

On the 30th of last month, the Junpu Bureau used the Lifei small steamer to transport a large sum of money to pay the salaries of the bureau's staff and servants. The money was robbed by thieves in the Pudong River, who shot and injured Chinese and foreign employees, killing two people. Afterwards, the police arrested many criminals. Because the Pudong River is under the jurisdiction of the inland government, several of the arrested criminals have been transferred to the Shanghai Local Court for investigation. On the 14th of this month, the Laozha Police Station arrested Zhang Genbao and Yao Zucheng from Pudong. Under interrogation, they confessed that one of their accomplices, Feng Qing, was hiding in Pudong. Chinese and foreign detectives secretly went to Pudong a few days ago and arrested Feng. He was brought to court yesterday morning. According to Feng, he only knew that they were going to rob land and accompanied them, but he did not do anything himself. Judge Zhou ordered the defendant to be detained and rescheduled the hearing.

Passenger Throws Himself into River Midstream 131

A Foolish Result, Disgraced and Ruined

Rescued by Fellow Passengers

At around 8:00 PM the day before yesterday, four men boarded Sampan No. 46 from the Hankou Road New Customs Wharf, intending to cross to Pudong. Upon interrogation, he confessed that his name was Guo Lianbiao, 21 years old, from Shaoxing, residing at No. 21 Zhilan Lane, French Concession. Because of his foolish nature, he had been repeatedly reprimanded by his father, but he still did not change. Eventually, he became disgraced and ruined and could not face anyone. Now he is suffering from a guilty conscience, so he threw himself into the river to commit suicide. The fellow passengers were my friends. The head of the police station said that his misfortune was self-inflicted and ordered his companions to take Guo home.

Xu Yan is Deceived and Loses her Virginity

Zhou Yungao Caught on the Way

Page 17

Education News

Special Report

Random Notes on Japanese Education 144

(6) (Hu Shuyi)

On the 5th, I went to observe the Second Higher Girls' School. This school is known for its physical education in Japan. There are approximately one thousand students. Each student is required to pay a certain amount for physical education. In addition to all kinds of sports equipment, there is a large swimming pool. Every day after 3 o'clock, students are compelled to exercise, including running, high jumping, ball games, and other competitive sports. Their outstanding achievements are the best in Japan. The most unusual thing is that during exercise, all students wear sportswear, consisting only of a tank top and shorts, no different from what men wear. The teachers at the school guide various sports and swimming exercises with great enthusiasm, showing no feminine affectation whatsoever. Such emphasis on physical education is not even surpassed by our country's specialized physical education schools. Following this, I was received by the city government, and with the permission of the Imperial Household Agency, I was able to visit the Imperial Palace in Japan. According to the ancient Kyoto Palace records, there are five locations: the Imperial Palace (御所), the Sento Imperial Palace (仙洞御所), the Nijo Detached Palace (二條離宫), the Katsura Detached Palace (桂離宫), and the Shugakuin Imperial Villa (修學院離宫). Due to time constraints, I only visited the Imperial Palace. The interior is extremely solemn. One palace depicts images of famous scholars and officials from the Tang and Song dynasties of our country, such as the hall where the Emperor received his vassals (天皇朝見諸候殿), the Shishinden Hall where the Emperor was enthroned (天皇就職加寃之紫宸殿), and the Seiryoden Hall where the Emperor relaxed (天皇游覽之清凉殿). Each was a sight to behold. The ancient customs and rituals refreshed my spirit. Afterwards, I went to the Kyoto Prefecture to inquire about educational matters in detail. I learned that there are 383 elementary schools, of which 86 are established by Kyoto City, while the rest are distributed to various districts. There are over 1.92 million children, and only about 800 children of school age are not enrolled. A majority of elementary school graduates continue their education. The average monthly salary for male teachers in elementary schools is 82 yuan, while for female teachers it is over 55 yuan. The average monthly salary for male specialist teachers in elementary schools is 57 yuan, while for female teachers it is 46 yuan. The average monthly salary for principals of lower elementary schools is 123 yuan, and for principals of complete elementary schools, it is 160 yuan. The total amount of annual seniority pay for elementary school teachers is over 37,000 yuan from the city and over 78,000 yuan from the county. All elementary school teachers in rural villages are provided with housing or housing subsidies. In order to encourage children to attend school, there are scholarship savings, with over 90,000 yuan allocated annually from the national treasury, and the remainder is planned by the prefecture. There are 68 public kindergartens and 51 private kindergartens in Kyoto Prefecture. In Japan, kindergartens are often separated from elementary schools and established independently, and the local government strongly encourages the establishment of private kindergartens. The Kyoto Prefectural Normal School has one school for men and one for women, each with two divisions and a specialized course for women. The Women's Normal School also has a nursery training institute, aiming to train kindergarten teachers. Kyoto Prefecture has eight middle schools, with a total of 135 classes. There are eleven private middle schools, with a total of 119 classes. The prefecture has eleven higher girls' schools, with a total of 143 classes. There are twelve private ones, with a total of 107 classes. The prefecture has sixteen vocational schools, and there are three private ones, with the majority being agricultural, followed by industrial. The prefecture has one medical university and one women's specialized school, divided into arts and science departments. In addition, there are schools for the blind and deaf, providing facilities for special education. As for Kyoto City, there are 22 kindergartens with 88 staff members and 2,429 children. There have been 1,674 graduates. There are 85 elementary schools with 1,750 staff members and 75,277 children. There have been over 130,000 graduates. There are ten vocational supplementary schools for girls, and one school each for the blind and deaf. There are thirteen girls' schools and middle schools each, and seven vocational schools, with 273 staff members and 4,795 students. The normal school has a one-year program, with 77 staff members, 972 students, and 255 graduates. There is one higher school, with 58 staff members and 979 students. There are fourteen specialized schools, with 523 staff members and 5,444 students. There are four private universities, with 340 staff members and 3,325 students. There are two public universities, with 631 staff members and 6,294 students. There have been 1,264 graduates. In addition, there is a commemorative zoo, housing 94 species of mammals, 1,099 species of birds, 136 species of reptiles, and 2 species of amphibians. There is also the Enshi Kyoto Museum, with 1,124 historical exhibits, 1,140 art exhibits, and 619 craft exhibits. All of these social educational facilities are particularly admirable to us.

Zhejiang Province Promulgates Methods for Holding

Courses on Phonetic Symbols in Each School District 148

The Zhejiang Provincial Department of Education considers phonetic symbols to be a powerful tool for unifying the national language and implementing mass education. Recently, it specially formulated a method for holding phonetic symbol training courses in each school district in the province, in order to provide sequential training. The government ordered each city and county to comply with the method, and also ordered the provincial middle schools to supervise the affiliated elementary schools to properly determine the method for holding phonetic symbol training courses in each school district, and to report the progress in detail for review. The methods for holding phonetic symbol training courses in each school district are as follows:

1. The phonetic symbol training courses in each school district shall be sponsored by the elementary schools affiliated with the provincial middle schools, and the Mandarin teachers of this middle school who have studied phonetic symbols will be responsible as lecturers to convene elementary school teachers and administrative personnel from each county and city in this school district for training. The training course will be named the Zhejiang Province No. ○ School District Phonetic Symbol Training Course.

2. Each county and city government must send at least four current elementary school teachers and administrative personnel from the county to attend the lectures. Their travel and food expenses will be provided by the respective organizations, but those who voluntarily attend must bear their own expenses, and should notify the affiliated elementary school in advance.

3. The training period is limited to one week. The opening date will be determined by each affiliated elementary school based on the situation in the school district, and the county and city governments will be notified.

4. The course distribution is as follows:

勹 Pronunciation Method 120 minutes

夊 Pronunciation Practice 240 minutes

口 Spelling Practice 240 minutes

匚 Tone Practice 120 minutes

万 Word and Sentence Practice 240 minutes

Calligraphy Practice 120 minutes

去 Note Past Practice 360 minutes

5. After the training period, the attendees from each county and city should return to their respective counties and cities to be responsible for publicity and explanation. The methods will be determined by each county and city.

6. The lecturers of the training course may be given appropriate honorariums, and the office staff may be given appropriate allowances. Other miscellaneous office expenses will be paid from the contingency fund of each middle school in the 18th or 19th year, but shall not exceed 100 yuan at most.

7. After the training course is completed, the affiliated elementary schools of each middle school should report the progress to the Department of Education for record.

Ministry of Education

Instructions to the Supervisory Office for Students Studying in Japan 149

Review and Approval of Qualifications of Graduates from University Preparatory Courses and Specialized Schools, etc. The Ministry of Education, based on the report from Wang Keren, the supervisor of students studying in Japan, requesting clarification on nine matters concerning students studying abroad, hereby selects and records several important matters on the left: (1) Should graduates of a two-year university preparatory course and graduates of a four-year specialized school have the same qualifications, or which is higher and has the priority to receive the Boxer Indemnity? (Ministry of Education Instructions) Graduates of a two-year university preparatory course and graduates of a four-year specialized school, the latter's qualifications are higher. (2) Was the former Beijing Sino-French University a national or private institution, and if private, has it been registered? (Ministry Order) The Sino-French University is a private institution, formally recognized by the former Beijing Ministry of Education, but has not yet been approved for registration by this Ministry. (3) Have Beijing Chaoyang and China Universities been registered? (Ministry Order) Neither Chaoyang nor China University has been approved for registration. (4) In the past, your Ministry stipulated the method for granting Boxer Indemnity to Class A female auditors, stipulating that in the future, female students who have equivalent qualifications to enter a university department, who attend university courses and whose performance is comparable to that of male students, should still be allowed to receive the Boxer Indemnity according to the Class B qualifications. Since female students cannot be considered as attending and being tested at the beginning of their studies, and it is also impossible to know whether their performance can be comparable to that of male students, can they still receive the Boxer Indemnity according to the Class B qualifications at this time? (Ministry Order) Testing includes various tests upon enrollment and during studies. The treatment of Class A female auditors is completely the same as that of undergraduate male students, which has been clearly explained in Instruction No. 937. (4) Currently, there are people who take advantage of the situation and try to obtain subsidies. They often hold official documents from local governments or schools granting subsidies of 400 yuan in order to obtain the qualifications of government-funded students and receive the Boxer Indemnity. It is proposed that your Ministry stipulate that in the future, those who receive subsidies from local governments or schools must submit a certificate of government-funded study abroad issued by the Department of Education of each province to the Ministry for approval before they can be considered as government-funded students. (Ministry Order) Those who receive certificates for self-funded study abroad, regardless of whether they have received subsidies from schools or other organizations, will be considered as self-funded students. (6) In the future, it is proposed to use the public Zhe telegraph code published by the Commercial Press for telegrams, which is more economical. (Ministry Order) It should be approved.

Recalling Overseas Chinese Education Rights in Taiwan

Petition Representatives Being Expelled from the Country 150

There are nearly 50,000 overseas Chinese in Taiwan. The education of their children has always been controlled by the Japanese government in Taiwan, who have been implementing a slave-like education. Conscious members of the overseas Chinese community have initiated the organization of a petition group to reclaim the rights to overseas Chinese education in Taiwan, and have elected Chen Renshan and others as representatives. They returned to the country in February and March of this year to petition, requesting the assistance of the Overseas Chinese Association in this port. The association immediately submitted the petition to the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission of the Central Government in Nanjing, as well as the Ministry of Education and the Ministry of Foreign Affairs of the National Government, requesting prompt approval. The representatives personally went to Beijing to petition and received approvals stating that after the Ministry of Foreign Affairs sends someone to Taiwan to establish a consulate, the matter will be handed over to the consul stationed in Taiwan for handling. However, it has been nearly four months since the Overseas Chinese Association received the approval, and the Ministry of Foreign Affairs has not yet sent anyone to Taiwan. It is also unknown how the overseas Chinese education there should be handled before the envoy is sent. Chen Renshan, one of the representatives who traveled long distances back to the country to petition, was rejected from returning to Taiwan due to this incident. The following is a brief account of Chen Renshan's expulsion: The Overseas Chinese Association recently received a letter from a certain overseas Chinese organization in Taiwan stating, "After investigation, Comrade Chen Renshan is extremely enthusiastic about overseas Chinese affairs and overseas Chinese education. It is a pity that he was deported as soon as he arrived in Taiwan. The reasons for his deportation can be described by Comrade Chen himself," etc. It also received a letter from Mr. Chen stating, "On May 10th, I departed from my hometown of Wenzhou with my family to go to Taiwan. I arrived in Fuzhou first, and on the 28th, I boarded the Daikyu Maru. I landed at Tamsui Port in Taiwan the next day. I went to Taipei on the same day and stayed briefly at the Chinese Association. Suddenly, many police detectives arrested me and took me to the Taipei Prefecture Police Department. They said that I was agitating the overseas Chinese in Taiwan, returning to the country to petition, etc., and claimed that I was an ideologically inappropriate person. They immediately issued an expulsion order. Because there was no ship available for export at the time, I was detained in the police station for three days. On June 1st, I was sent to Keelung and placed in the bottom of the hold of the Daikyu Maru for about six hours. I only gained freedom after the ship set sail. I arrived in Fuzhou again the next day. The humiliation of me personally by the Taiwan authorities this time is purely the Japanese imperialists' oppression of the cultural movement of overseas Chinese in Taiwan, so that all our overseas Chinese will be enslaved by them. Since 1926, the Taiwan authorities have expelled more than a hundred overseas Chinese intellectuals. This not only destroys the cultural movement of overseas Chinese, but also insults our national dignity. Which citizen does not hate this? I have long admired your association's enthusiasm for overseas Chinese affairs. I dare to ask you to submit this matter to your association. At the same time, I hope that the newspapers in Shanghai will publish this matter in detail so that the people of the country will know the situation of overseas Chinese in Taiwan," etc. Based on this, the association immediately submitted it again to the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission and the Ministry of Education, urging the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to negotiate with Japan and send someone to Taiwan to protect the overseas Chinese and assist in overseas Chinese education as soon as possible. It is hoped that the diplomatic authorities will take concrete measures.

County Education Bureau Holds Elementary School Examination 155

The Shanghai County Education Bureau held this year's senior graduation examination and junior completion examination for various elementary schools. The curriculum meeting has decided to continue to handle it according to the previous session's methods. The methods for this session have also been drafted. The examination subjects are high school, junior high, party principles, national language, arithmetic, and general knowledge. The dates are June 30th for high school and July 6th for junior high (no change in case of wind or rain). The time is 90 minutes for high school national language, 40 minutes for general knowledge in the morning, 40 minutes for party principles and 60 minutes for arithmetic in the afternoon. The time is 45 minutes for junior high national language, 40 minutes for general knowledge in the morning, and 40 minutes for party principles and 60 minutes for arithmetic in the afternoon. There will be a 10-minute break after each subject. Lunch will be handled by the school at the gathering place, with meals or snacks provided for the number of students taking the test, limited to one small yuan per person. Graduation standards: Each school must conduct its own examinations for each subject, and only those who pass the bureau's examination can graduate. Examination grade reports: Each school prepares its own examination grade reports for each subject, and submits them to the bureau in due course after settlement (the size and format of the grade report must be in accordance with the bureau's issuance). The bureau will print and distribute the examination grade reports to each school in advance, register the names of the students taking the test this year, and hand them over to the invigilators on the day of the examination.

Chengzhong Middle School Holds Calligraphy Competition 157

In order to encourage students to practice calligraphy, Chengzhong Middle School in this port holds a school-wide calligraphy competition once a year, divided into preliminary and final rounds. The preliminary round is judged by calligraphers within the school, and 30 students are selected for the final round. The final round is judged by calligraphers outside the school, and 10 students are selected from the preliminary round. Famous calligraphers in Shanghai, such as Wu Changshuo, Zeng Nongran, and Yang Liaogong, have all served as judges for the school. This year, the school invited Ma Gongyu, a professor of epigraphy and calligraphy at the China Academy of Arts and Literature, to serve as the final round judge. He examined each student with one paper each of large and small regular script, and selected 10 students, including Tan Shao. The first to fourth place winners were awarded gold and silver medals, and the fifth and below were awarded books and stationery. Professor Ma Gongyu also gave each student rubbings of his own calligraphy.

Sports

A Few Opinions on Preparing for the National Games by Wu Yunrui 163

In early April, during the National Games held in Hangzhou, it was heard that the Central Government had resolved to allocate 500,000 yuan for the capital to prepare for the next National Games. Before long, Yan and Feng raised troops, betraying the Central Government. Military affairs were pressing, and the economy was exhausted. Even in this turbulent time, the preparatory work for the National Games is still being actively carried out, which proves the Central Government's determination to build and its keenness to promote sports. All of us in the sports community should do our best to contribute our ideas to make this event perfect. Now that the preparatory committee has been announced and the chief and deputy secretaries have been appointed, the preparatory work, with its myriad details, will soon begin. As far as I can see, the most important thing is the construction of sports facilities. In beautiful and advanced countries, major cities all have magnificent and advanced stadiums, comparable to libraries and other public buildings. Now, the capital's stadium is chosen next to Linggu Temple, close to Dr. Sun Yat-sen's Mausoleum, which clearly intends to be as beautiful as Dr. Sun Yat-sen's Mausoleum and be called a major central building. Its form and structure must be legal and beautiful, which goes without saying. Although I am not an engineer, I have observed sports architecture abroad and have done some research on implementation. Based on my sense of civic duty, I would like to discuss it with the preparatory committee.

(1) Construction Funding 164

The cost of sports construction can range from millions to hundreds of thousands. The budget for the next National Games is a total of 500,000 yuan, which is not enough if it is all used for construction. Therefore, all hospitality expenses should be minimized. According to the previous National Games, the hospitality expenses were no more than 30,000 yuan. Therefore, 50,000 to 60,000 yuan is enough for the next National Games, and the remaining 400,000 yuan can be used for construction.

(2) Location of the Stadium 165

The location of the stadium should be chosen in a place with convenient transportation and easy access for the public, so that it is convenient for daily use and can be enjoyed more often. If it is only for the National Games and does not consider the convenience of daily use, the effectiveness of the stadium will be minimal. Even if the architecture is exquisite, it will be in vain. Now, the location of the next National Games stadium has been selected next to Linggu Temple in the east of Dr. Sun Yat-sen's Mausoleum, taking into account its large area, beautiful scenery, and future urban construction plans, which is quite reasonable. However, it is too far from the city. It may be acceptable for people in cities with convenient transportation and families with cars, but not for Nanjing, which has inconvenient transportation, and the increasingly impoverished people of the Republic of China. Moreover, now that the civil war has restarted, construction has stopped, and there are still many vacant lots in the city. With financial difficulties and high construction costs, the construction outside the city is indefinite, and the stadium will have collapsed long before people move out of the city. This is also something that cannot but be considered. Although the location of the stadium has already been decided and cannot be reversed, why can't the swimming pool be located in a suitable place in the city, such as near the Lizhi Society and the public stadium? After the Games, tickets can be purchased to enter the pool, which can start a new trend of recreation for citizens. If the economy is insufficient, an outdoor swimming pool can be opened behind the afforestation office, using the spring water from Zijin Mountain as the pool water. In this way, the water will be automatically changed, which can save the cost of changing water on weekdays, like the outdoor swimming pool in IronClale, Missouri, USA, is a good example. A year ago, I led the Boy Scouts to camp next to this spring and had this idea. The cost of opening the spring is at most 10,000 yuan, which I hope the authorities will pay attention to.

(3) Allocation of Venues 166

The venues must be divided into main and auxiliary venues. The main venue must be able to hold track and field events, football, volleyball, basketball, and other important events. The surrounding area must be built with bleachers. Like the stadium outside the Meiji Jingu Shrine in Japan, one side of the bleachers should be built and the other three sides should be built with grass slopes to save money. If the foothills can be used in Linggu Temple, it will be more economical. The bleachers should be able to accommodate at least 100,000 people. Because there are too many teams, auxiliary venues for basketball, football, volleyball, tennis, etc. can be built next to the main venue. If the economy is insufficient, there is no need to build bleachers. The next National Games venue should use all its financial resources to operate the main venue and not repeat the mistakes of the Hangzhou stadium by building bleachers in the auxiliary venues as well.

(4) Practical Issues of Construction 167

A. There are two types of running track forms: normal and curved (Korbogenform), and modified (including semi-circular and pointed circular). The stadiums of the German Sports University and the Amsterdam Stadium in the Netherlands all use the normal form to ensure that a legal football field can be built in the middle of the track. This spring, when I visited the construction of the Hangzhou stadium, the sand pits and runways were arbitrarily arranged inside the track without any rules, resulting in the football field being completely occupied. All important football matches cannot be played in this main venue. In the last few days, this venue was deserted, which greatly damaged the spirit of the Games.

B. The construction of the track itself is not a simple matter. It is usually divided into three layers. There are many formulas for the material of the upper layer, mainly composed of fine white coal ash, clay, and sand. It is definitely not something that can be done with pure fine coal ash. The long jump record in the previous National Games was at most 6.05 meters, which was due to the illegal construction of the long jump runway. The construction of the new stadium in the capital this time may also be the venue for the eleventh Far Eastern Games, and also the future World Games. It is related to the observation of both Chinese and foreigners. The preparatory authorities should pay attention to it.

C. The arrangement of the runways and throwing areas should avoid being inside the football field, which will destroy the football field. The Hangzhou National Games venue made this mistake. Germany is the most sophisticated in the construction of sports architecture. The high jump, long jump sand pit, and runway are all allocated inside the curved section of the track and outside the football field. If the north and south are not conducive to the wind, you can abandon this and choose that. The arrangement of the throwing areas in the Meiji Jingu Shrine stadium in Japan is modeled after Germany. I hope the preparatory authorities will pay attention to it.
