Free Talk

Dismissed with a Laugh by Haike 172

A: Last time, when I was on a ship with my wife crossing the sea, she accidentally fell into the sea on the deck. A shark swam up, looked at her, and then turned its tail and left, without eating her.

B: A narrow escape is a blessing in disguise. Your wife has boundless blessings. But why was that shark so civilized?

A: It probably had the same problem as me. As soon as it saw her face, it was frightened.

Passenger A on the tram: Hey, friend, I stood up to give my seat to this female passenger. Why did you sit down so impolitely?

Passenger B on the tram: It doesn't matter. This female passenger is my wife. We can accommodate each other in everything.

Father: My child, you should do everything with your heart. The more hardships you endure, the more likely you will reach the top in the future.

Son: Father, but what if I dig a well?

Customer: What is the price for taking pictures of children?

Photographer: Five yuan per dozen.

Customer: I'm sorry. I only have eleven children now. I'll come again when my wife gives birth to another one next year.

Talking About Airspace Issues by Huang Jiping 173

Meteorological work is one of the most important sciences. All European and American countries are vigorously promoting it. The authorities do not hesitate to invest heavily in its operation and construction. There are meteorological stations and observatories on mountaintops, seashores, and in major trading ports. They recruit experts to devote themselves to their work. Their efforts are great, and their achievements are remarkable. Therefore, the discovery of stars and the observation of weather conditions are frequently reported in newspapers. Their influence on farmers, industrialists, and merchants is great. Our country's industries are backward, and even in this meteorological aspect, sovereignty has long been lost. How many of the famous astronomical institutions in the country are not controlled by others? It is lamentable to say. Since the establishment of the Institute of Meteorology and the Institute of Astronomy by the Academia Sinica, Chinese people have begun to pay attention. However, in the early stages, there is a shortage of talent, and it is important to seek expansion. The cultivation of talent is even more urgent. Do we not see that foreigners in the northeast and northwest border areas are ambitiously planning to overstep their authority? My friend Huang Xiaqian is a scholar of meteorology. He followed Dr. Zhu Kezhen in assisting with the work of the Institute of Meteorology in his early years. He is now teaching meteorology and climate courses at Tsinghua University and is preparing for a large-scale meteorological station. Recently, he talked with reporters about the crisis of China's airspace problem, which is quite alarming. I hereby explain it to the readers.

He said: The meteorological business seems to be gradually developing in our country. The airspace problem, which has not been paid attention to for a long time, may gradually enter the minds of Chinese people. It cannot be said that it is not a good phenomenon in recent years. However, the foundation of our country's meteorological business is very weak. The area of ​​the United States is comparable to ours. There are more than 3,170 large and small meteorological stations and observatories in the country. The annual expenses reach more than 2 million gold yuan. (approximately 8 million yuan in our country) The degree of development of Japan's meteorological business is not inferior to that of Europe and the United States in terms of area. In 1919, a marine meteorological station was added in Kobe. The construction cost was 400,000 yuan, of which 230,000 yuan was donated by the shipping industry. The recognition of the meteorological business by its people is also commendable. In recent years, a high-altitude meteorological station has been added in Tateyama near Tokyo for the purpose of researching aviation. The construction cost is 100,000 yuan. The scale is not small. The current meteorological business in our country cannot be compared with the United States and Japan. In terms of area, it cannot be compared with any small country in the world. Because our government does not know how to handle it, it allows foreigners to overstep their authority. The establishment of the Xujiahui Observatory by French priests is early and well-known. Most of the 47 customs weather stations are also managed by foreigners. Japan regards Manchuria as its operating area, so it has established a meteorological station in Dalian, Lushun, Yingkou, Liaoning, and Changchun. I have not seen any response from the Chinese people. Recently, Sven Hedin (transliteration), a Swede, privately established four meteorological stations in Xinjiang in the name of archaeology. (Ruoqiang, Dihua, Hami, Kuqa) After several years of observation, the records have been obtained. It has now been mailed to Germany for future aviation reference. These are all noteworthy events in the history of our country in recent years.

From this, it can be seen that foreigners' intentions to harm our country are obvious. If the Chinese people continue to kill each other and refuse to wake up, I really have infinite worries and cannot solve them.

A Twelve-Year-Old Girl Giving Birth by Chance 174

Lost

There is a Chinese man named Bai Yongfu in Beixiadong 3rd Street, Xinyizhou, Korea. He is about 30 years old and is from Fushan, Shandong. Three years ago, he went to Korea to find work and lived there. He has been a carpenter for a living. After many years he'd saved some money. Last year, in January, he hired a matchmaker and betrothed a woman named Liu from the same hometown. The woman was twelve years old. Her biological father packed up and returned home. Bai welcomed the woman to his home to raise her. But dry firewood is close to fire, and he had long since actually carried out the role of foster parent. Unexpectedly, the lotus room dripped dew, and a pearl fetus was formed. By March of this year, she was pregnant for ten months. She gave birth to a son in one fell swoop. However, Bai suffered from excessive labor and developed hemoptysis. After three or four months, it did not work. By the middle of last month, he died. The young widow's life is difficult. She is looking for a good husband to prepare for another marriage.

Outside the east gate of Bu Kui, Heilongjiang Province, there was an old couple of Henan disaster victims last month. They led a boy and a girl. The girl was holding a child. They sat on the ground. There were many spectators at that time. A busybody asked about the surname and address. The old woman said that her surname was Wang and she was from Gushi County, Henan Province. The boy and girl are her son and daughter-in-law. The child held by the girl is her grandson. She also asked how old the boy and girl were. She replied that they were both twelve years old. She asked why they got married at the age of twelve. The old woman smiled and did not answer. Then she saw the child crying in her arms. The girl randomly breastfed him. The onlookers gave him hundreds of Jiang Qian. The old woman thanked him and left. Looking closely at the young couple, they were small and thin. The so-called twelve years old is definitely not a false statement. The development of human reproduction can also be seen from this. (But thank you)

One Evening's Talk with a Returnee from Japan by Bing 175

My old classmate Yang Jun has studied in Japan for ten years and has recently returned to China. He invited me to his hotel to talk late into the night. Many of the things we talked about are worth recording. I will write down two or three of them.

Yang Jun said that the Chinese side failed in the Tokyo Far Eastern Games. Although it was due to the unfairness of the Japanese referees and the lack of coordinated action training of our athletes, the fact is that Chinese education does not pay enough attention to sports. Someone suggested to the Ministry of Education that elementary schools should also be equipped with sports fields. Although it cannot be realized due to the current economic strength, it must be carried out in practice within the possible scope to cultivate a general national habit of paying attention to sports. Japanese elementary schools attach great importance to sports. The country has always regarded worshiping Bushido as its national soul, that is, the so-called Yamato soul. Elementary school students also use sword fighting as a game. The sword is made of bamboo or wood. They stab each other, stare, and puff out their chests, just like a samurai.

The Japanese like martial arts. Suicide is also heroic. Whether it is for economic reasons, love, or ethics, suicides are often reported in the newspapers. When they die, they either cut their stomachs, lie on the train tracks, or jump off high cliffs. Occasionally, they also drown themselves. There are few who die by hanging or taking anesthetics. Previously, Ryunosuke Akutagawa committed suicide, stating that he did so because he felt a hazy unease. He did not want to make people uncomfortable, so he took eye drops. The Japanese ridiculed him, saying that artists are not afraid of being born ugly, but they must not die beautifully. It can be said that the Japanese nation is inherently cruel, and suicide is also carried out in a cruel way.

Finally, Yang Jun showed me the public notice of the managers of students studying in Japan from various provinces, which was issued in response to a reporter from a Shanghai newspaper who commented on the affairs of studying in Japan. This led to a discussion of the history of studying in Japan and the issue of studying abroad. In 1905, the Japanese Ministry of Education issued regulations on the control of Qing and Korean students. Chen Tianhua, a student from Hunan, committed suicide by jumping into the sea because of this. All the students returned to China and established China Public School in Shanghai.

A Letter Regarding Criticism of Mei Lanfang (Middle) Zhi 176

The Western newspapers say that beauty cannot fully understand Mei's drama, and they have issued five miles of fog. If wisdom is not equal, how can it be forced to be the same? Those who do not deeply understand beauty have such a proposition, while those who understand it, such as Stork Young, have more than twenty articles published in the New York World and other newspapers. They have thoroughly analyzed the subtle points of Mei's performance. It has been translated and will be dedicated to you in a special publication soon. After reading it, you will know that there are many who understand it. Mr. Mei's trip is to get all the American yellow-haired and white-haired old people to dance with excitement. The situation is somewhat impossible, and those around him may not use this to be harsh. The theory of male women is viewed by those who value men over women and despise actors. It is not a compliment. However, in terms of words, Zhang Liang is like a woman, and Xie Lanfang has no frivolous meaning at all. Moreover, those around you have gained expertise in Western learning. They must know that foreign newspapers like to create strange words to attract attention, such as calling former French Prime Minister Clemenceau a tiger. Even drawing a cartoon of him is also a Yan Han and a tiger head, which is the same principle. If you must say that Mr. Mei's role is Dan, then not only is it true in China, but also in European dramas, it has always been the case that Bian becomes hairpin. Even now, the old habits have not disappeared. When Mr. Mei was in the United States, he met a Dan actor. It is not surprising that they looked at each other with their eyes. Why is it so precious? The word idol is very appropriate. Mr. Mei is not worthy of being worshiped by the Chinese people. However, I believe that the theory of the concentration of modern Chinese people's thoughts is that the worshipers should be famous figures in politics? Those who are alive are ruining the country every day, and those who are dead are spreading false theories. Should they be famous generals in the military? They are brave in internal wars but timid in national crises. Should they be famous scholars in academia? Those who hold on to the old only engage in plagiarism, and those who admire the new only engage in purchasing. Think about it with a calm mind. Mr. Mei has become famous with a skill. He has been studying hard for ten years, and he still feels that he is more virtuous than them. Those around you have been holding on to themselves in the morning. They have counted the characters of modern times and recorded their omissions. They should not regard my words as irrelevant. As for the words representing Oriental art, Mr. Mei has never claimed it. Even if there are exaggerated words, they are from the mouths of others, not Mr. Mei's responsibility. You quoted the Associated Press telegram, which also refers to drama. Why do you say that here? In the past, it was said that he represented the figures worshiped by the Chinese people. Mr. Mei has never dreamed of it. If the Chinese people can completely abandon the thought of fame and profit, do not fall under the power of money, and do not hesitate to blindly follow the path of novelty, but only devote themselves to literature and drama, and cultivate their minds, it is already a good thing. The word worship does not specifically refer to people with fame and leadership. Moreover, it does not match the original text. Then what is the meaning of the so-called "hard to close your eyes" and "Isn't it wrong?" When this news was heard in the country, there were many criticisms. Originally, there is no absolute theory of agreement in the universe, and what you have cited should be the speculation of boring people and the short comments to fulfill their responsibilities. You have been in the newspaper industry, so you have used the tools of quickly collecting money and the titles of digging wells when you are thirsty as a model to show that it is public opinion. Isn't it too silly? The Tianjin Ta Kung Pao has always been praised by the Chinese people for its comments. It once published a theory to praise Mr. Mei's success. The original text is in the Humanities Library and should be compiled for review. Then you will know that public opinion is not completely biased towards your instructions.

Hai. In 1915, all the students studying in Japan returned to China due to the 21 demands diplomatic issue raised by Japan. In 1918, all the students studying in Japan returned to China due to the military agreement issue. They also founded the National Salvation Daily in Shanghai. In 1928, the Jinan incident occurred, and most of the students studying in Japan returned to China. Scholars and politicians in the Japanese education circle often wondered why Chinese students studying in Japan engaged in anti-Japanese movements, which were even more intense than the general Chinese people. They did not know that the students studying in Japan stayed in that country and heard and saw the most stimulating things, so their anti-Japanese sentiments were also more intense. This is an inevitable trend.

Japan has the most students studying abroad, followed by the United States. There are many reasons for this relationship. Some people say that there are many students studying in Japan because of its proximity, the same language, the short time, the low cost, and the unstable political situation in China. The former Ministry of Education said that there are many students studying in the United States because it is easy to enter American schools and they can attend classes with domestic academic qualifications. Many of them return to China with graduation qualifications in less than two or three years, so self-funded students flock to them. In 1919, the German mark depreciated, and the number of students studying in Germany increased day by day. In 1920, there were more than 1,000 students studying in France and Germany. In 1923, German social life gradually recovered, and the number of students decreased day by day. There were also fewer people going to France. In the past, there were as many as 10,000 students studying in Japan during the crash course era. Recently, it has gradually decreased to 3,400 to 500 people. All of these can give us a glimpse of the reasons for the rise and fall of our students studying in various countries.

Heart's Warmth (217) by Bao Tianxiao 177

Chapter 12: Farewell Banquet, Parting Feast, Plucking Flowers to Keep a Beautiful Image; Famous Garden Gathering, Tea Tasting to Admire Lovely Features

Well, even though they waited a long time in vain, it was still considered losing at sunrise and gaining at sunset. The attendants busily began their roles, offering hot towels and lemon tea, their smiling faces conveying greetings and flattery. After a flurry of activity, A Jin was "more talk than rice porridge," while Ruiyun simply smiled silently. She was wearing a new light blue silk jacket embroidered with many black swallows. Her hair was styled in a fashionable bun, adorned with a red cactus flower. Her face was powdered snow-white, and the rouge extended from her cheeks to her eyelids. Her beauty was like a flower in early spring, and she constantly smiled. Zuo Shichen thought to himself, "Good, the 'golden gate of her heart' is now slightly ajar." Seeing her smile, he knew that she felt no displeasure. Looking at her flushed face and deep red lips, he knew she was preparing to be a bride. He sat at the head of a somewhat rectangular dining table, with A Jin on his right and Ruiyun on his left. He gazed at her for a moment and said, "You're especially beautiful today." Ruiyun didn't say anything, just smiled. A Jin said, "This fabric was a gift from Mr. Cheng. Our eldest aunt would never wear such clothes." Shichen asked, "Which Mr. Cheng?" Ruiyun replied, "You know him, the old Mr. Cheng from the Portland Cement Company. His concubine is one of our little sisters." Zuo Shichen nodded and asked, "Why did you style your hair today?" Ruiyun said, "Hurry up, I'm starving. Order for me." Zuo Shichen smiled, feeling that although her answer didn't address his question, his question didn't have much basis either. If she was happy to style her hair, she styled her hair; if she was happy to braid it, she braided it. Their complaints about being hungry were the real issue. They left the theater at six o'clock and had been running around outside without going home, so of course they were hungry. People often forget practical matters with empty talk. Whether or not to style hair is empty talk, while being hungry is a practical matter. So he casually picked up a menu and asked, "Well, what do you want to eat? Tell me, and I'll write it down for you." Ruiyun asked, "Do you think I look better with styled hair or braids?" Zuo Shichen laughed, "I asked you why you styled your hair, and you didn't answer me, just complained about being hungry. Now that I'm asking you to order, you're asking me about the hair and braids." Ruiyun said, "Tell me what you think." Zuo Shichen said, "Both look good. Ugly people look ugly with braids, and even uglier with styled hair. Pretty people look good with braids, and even better with styled hair." Ruiyun pouted and said, "You're always like this, never telling the truth when I ask you something." Zuo Shichen was exasperated, "Hey, isn't that the truth?" A Jin said, "No, that's what our eldest aunt said. Little Miss often wears braids, but when she goes to someone's mansion, she can't wear braids anymore, so she's getting used to styling her hair first, so her hair will be softer."

Settlement of Cotton Price Limits 188

New Transactions Not Allowed Below Minimum Settlement Price

Bombay Dispatch, 19th - The East India Cotton Association has issued another notice regarding minimum settlement prices to its members. The text is as follows: The notice of the minimum cotton settlement price was issued on June 10th. It is now known that many holders of forward contracts for July and August have been unable to settle their contracts. To facilitate settlement, it is hereby notified that the settlement price may be agreed upon by both buyers and sellers. The settlement of contracts entered into before June 9th may also be handled in this manner. New transactions for the July and August forward contracts are not allowed to be established below the minimum settlement price set by the Association. Members are requested to pay attention. According to the minimum prices set on June 10th: Old cotton, Bengal, July, 175 Rupees; Broach, July and August, 240 Rupees; Oomra, July, 197 Rupees; New cotton, Bengal, December and January, 185 Rupees; Broach, April and May, 250 Rupees; Oomra, December and January, 207 Rupees.

Rising Rice Prices in the Riverfront Rice Market 189

Top White Rice Reaches 23 Yuan Outside the Customs

Yesterday, very few rice boats arrived at the wharves in Zhabei. Rice shops in this area, due to gradually dwindling stockpiles, have shown increased interest in purchasing. The price of white rice has been rising sharply, with top-grade rice already reaching 23 yuan outside the customs in off-market trading. Officially, regular rice has virtually no transactions, while central rice is generally quoted at around 22 yuan. Even second-grade rice is trading at 21 yuan, with the lowest at 20 yuan and a half, a sharp increase of more than 0.3 yuan compared to the previous market. Current riverfront stockpiles are dwindling. Although the Social Bureau has strictly enforced regulations, market transactions remain the same. Moreover, this high price of 23 yuan is a new record for the port. As the early rice has arrived in small quantities and sales are brisk, prices have increased by 0.01 or 0.02 yuan. A small amount of premium glutinous rice has been offered on the market, and the market is stable. The price of foreign rice has also been reported to be high, with a rapid increase of 0.5 yuan or even 1 yuan, reaching 19.4 yuan. ▲Sources of rice from the Shanghai South area are very scarce. Premium Changshu rice and Xichang rice have not arrived in port. Rice shops in Suzhou and Tongzhou are doing small-scale retail sales and are unusually diligent, but unfortunately there are no large quantities in stock to meet the market demand. The prices of various types of rice have generally increased. The market here mainly deals in medium-grade rice, so the prices differ slightly from the North area. However, rice from Tongli also costs around 20 yuan. The market for early rice in the South area is brisk, but rice from Tongzhou, Changzhou, and other areas is scarce in Shanghai. Only a small amount remains in warehouses, and merchants are holding onto their goods to speculate. The price of premium goods is also quoted at 19 plus yuan, and there is a slight indication of private trading. The market atmosphere is very active, and prices are also thriving. ▲Rice market news from Wuxi: The supply of rough rice and rice paddy in Wuxi has been dwindling in recent days, and the overall stock has been greatly reduced. Recently, merchants from Changshu have come to Wuxi to purchase rice, causing the market price of rough rice to soar to 17 yuan, which has affected the Shanghai rice market. However, it is said that the supply of japonica rice in Changshu is about to run out, so they have had to turn to neighboring counties to purchase it, and are also hoping for foreign rice to supplement the supply.

Flour and Wheat Market After the Order to Stabilize Prices 190

The spot flour price fluctuated higher, while futures prices for all months decreased. Yesterday, the flour market presented a trend of near-term price declines and stable long-term prices. The surge in prices over the past week has been excessive. Although partly due to the high cost of raw materials and the lack of stock at factories, much of it was fueled by market sentiment due to the nature of the exchange. One side used its manipulative tactics, while the other took advantage of the factories' reluctance to sell, leading to repeated price hikes, reaching the highest levels ever seen. Yesterday, due to the Social Bureau's strict order to stabilize prices, and the exchange's increase in margin requirements and shortening of the payment period, most speculative long positions without real backing have been restrained. Due to the margin requirement, they had to gradually unwind their positions, thus greatly easing the situation of runaway price increases. If the supply of wheat can increase and the factories can release more stock, the market may be stabilized. As a result of the closing: this month's price was down 0.0275 yuan from the previous day, July was down 0.015 yuan, August was down 0.0125 yuan, September was down 0.0075 yuan, October was down 0.01 yuan, and November was down 0.0025 yuan.

Wheat futures slightly declined, spot sales were active. Yesterday, wheat futures showed a trend of leveling off and fatigue. Most speculative longs, fearing the strict orders from the Social Bureau and sensing that new supplies were arriving, seemed unwilling to push prices higher. Therefore, those who had made profits unwound their positions. Although the consolidated price of foreign wheat has not yet been communicated, the quoted prices have fallen within one yuan. Therefore, if the exchange rate can improve, it may also be a turning point for the wheat market. As a result, June, September, and October were each down 0.02 yuan from the previous day, July and November were each down 0.04 yuan, and August was down 0.03 yuan. The spot wheat market is trending stable, as factories have good purchasing intentions and supplies are not very active. The opening price of Yellow Buckwheat was 5.05 yuan per 50 kg, Shaobo wheat was 5.1 yuan, Shuangfeng wheat was 5.08 yuan, Gaoyou wheat was 4.975 to 4.93 yuan, Wuhe wheat was 5.13 yuan, totaling 1,760 bags. Shaoxing wheat was 5.1 yuan, Guandian wheat was 5.13 yuan, Yangzhou wheat was 4.93 yuan, Chongming wheat was 4.77 yuan, and Jiangbei wheat was 4.8 yuan to 4.85 yuan, Jiading wheat was 4.87 to 4.85 yuan, Jiangwan wheat was 4.85 yuan, Yuepu wheat was 4.75 yuan, and Pudong wheat was 4.7 yuan, totaling 10,000 bags. The opening price of old wheat from various sources was 5.4 yuan per 50 kg, totaling 1,500 bags, which were allocated to various factories for processing.

Willing but Unable -

The Problem of Young People Seeking Education by Zhi Jing 198

School will soon be out for the summer, and we can hear the sound of "it's hard to study" everywhere. We can also see young people who are willing but unable to study, sighing and worrying that they don't know where they will get tuition for the next semester. Therefore, we will see countless young people who are forced to take detours, to bury their talents, and to abandon their proper path. This is such a painful thing! In fact, the founding fathers of the party and the country are shouting that youth are the essence of the country, the original vigor of the country, and the government should do its best to cultivate young people's good character and learning in order to consolidate the foundation of the party and the country. This is such a moving tone, this is how it should be! But why are there countless young people who are not able to study? Is it that these young people are willingly falling, or is it that the government has not made efforts to pay attention to the problem of young people seeking education? I regret that I have not received a report that proves this, so I dare not assume that my assumption is correct, so I have to remain in a state of doubt.

However, "schools are important places, and the poor should not enter." On the gates of those towering universities, there seem to be two strict and terrifying tiger-head plaques nailed invisibly, telling us poor boys that we have no choice but to lament in vain. Private schools are not worth mentioning. Even the most famous Central University, which was founded and maintained by the government with huge amounts of funding, still requires each student to have at least two to three hundred yuan per year to supplement it in order to study there, which is not feasible for young people from families with limited means to enjoy. Although the government has worked hard to establish several free schools, such as Shanghai Labor University, can these few free schools accommodate all young people who are willing but unable to study? In fact, we can still hear the sound of sighing that it is difficult to study everywhere, and we can see young people who are willing but unable to study worrying that they still don't know where they will get tuition for the next semester.

We all know that the large number of young people who are not able to study is an unfortunate state of social phenomenon. However, in our country, which is backward in industry, the manifestation of this social pathology can also be regarded as inevitable in fact. This is of course a whole social problem, but at least I personally believe that the urgent need to relieve the problem of being unable to study seems to be more important than other pathologies. It seems that this is a fundamental way to treat the problem. Young people are the essence of the country, the original vigor of the country, and genius is not necessarily the children of wealthy families, so if we want to save the country, we must do fundamental work, irrigate the essence of the country, cultivate the original vigor of the country, and provide as much as possible for the development of genius. In other words, we should try to relieve the young people from the despair of dropping out of school, so that those who are willing to study can reach the point where they can study if they are willing.

I regret that I have not thoroughly explored and analyzed various aspects of this issue, so I cannot offer a detailed relief plan. However, seeing the large number of young people who are unable to study, I have issued this call, hoping to elicit the sympathy of the general public, pay attention to this issue, and discuss fundamental and appropriate relief methods. I hope even more that the government will increase education funding as much as possible, so that national and provincial schools can provide free education to the poor, and provide economic assistance to private schools to reduce tuition fees, giving young people the possibility of "studying if they are willing." This is our hope, and this is our request.

Professor Brandte Resigns 199

The female professor of Guanghua University, Professor Bradly, is now going to resign. Her resignation letter states that she is returning to her home country to recuperate, but according to what we know, the real reason for her resignation is that she was ridiculed by the students at the Guanghua Fifth Anniversary Recreational Meeting. However, her tolerance is too narrow. Because of this small reason, she cried for two nights and now has sacrificed her position, which is not worth it. The day before yesterday evening, eight male and female students from the fourth grade set up a banquet in a restaurant to bid her farewell. The students felt reluctant to part with her because of the years of teacher-student relationship. The professor, although somewhat saddened, ultimately resigned because she was unwilling to be ridiculed. In short, although the professor has a narrow tolerance, it is also because she cherishes her reputation. (Bi)

Jiaotong University Improves Examination Method 200

Jiaotong University in this port has always been strict with term exams, and has specially organized an Examination Committee, with the deans of each college and the directors of each department as members, to take overall charge of all examination matters. For this exam, the Ministry of Railways has decided to send personnel to invigilate, and at the same time, the committee will also have multiple invigilators to assist on site, so the situation of this exam will be more serious than in previous sessions. The Examination Committee now, in view of the previous method of one week of review and one week of exams, believes that this is detrimental to the health of the students. The former method caused students to become mentally scattered during the review period, and they could not review all the subjects. After the review period was over, there was an exam every day during the exam period. As a result, those who embraced Buddhism temporarily all studied day and night, neglecting food and sleep, in order to pass the exam. Now, in the summer, it is extremely easy to cause illness. In order to improve this, Director Qiu Weiyu, Chairman of the Examination Committee, proposed to the Academic Affairs Meeting that, starting this session, the review and exam periods would be combined, with one exam every other day, still finishing in two weeks. Students can rest and recover from fatigue after the exam, which is greatly beneficial to health. During the rest period, they can also review the subjects to be tested the next day. Teachers can also grade the papers in a leisurely manner without being in a hurry, which is a win-win situation. The graduation class of this exam will be held from June 9th to 21st, and the non-graduation class from the 16th to the 28th, both for two weeks. (Wei)

Page 29

Social News

The Future of Black Americans 202

Black Americans have historically been oppressed by white Americans. It was not until Lincoln emancipated the slaves that they gained formal freedom. However, the discrimination against blacks in the southern states is still very obvious, and atrocities are often heard of. It was not until recent years, due to the struggles of the blacks themselves, that the situation has gradually improved. The London Observer recently published a dispatch from Alabama (the state in the southern United States where black education is most developed), which recorded the talk given by Dr. Morton, the president of Tuskegee University in Tuskegee, a famous black educator, during Black History Week. He described in detail the current situation and future of blacks in various parts of the United States, and there are many points worth noting. The following is a summary:

The future of blacks in the United States, although there are many difficulties and misfortunes, is generally very optimistic. It can even be said that there has never been such hope as there is today. Although black Americans, especially in the South, are still often discriminated against or deprived of their right to vote, most of this is due to the blacks themselves disregarding their rights, which cannot be entirely blamed on the authorities. Even white Americans in the southern states are prone to abandoning their rights.

As for black education, the tuition fees donated by various parties are now more than ever. It must be known that the southern states have only recently believed that education should be popularized. Decades ago, even poor white children did not have the right to enjoy education, let alone blacks. Now, the number of black schools is gradually increasing, and the number of blacks receiving education is also increasing rapidly. After graduating, many are able to engage in various professional occupations, not falling behind the whites. Generally speaking, the North has more doctors, lawyers, scientists, writers, and artists, while the South has more businessmen. Now, the National Black Businessmen's Association has more and more members and is making more and more progress in its affairs. I am honored to be the president of the association and know many people with great vision and extraordinary knowledge. Blacks are mostly engaged in banking, insurance, and manufacturing. Even women are quite talented, such as Mrs. Walker, who is the president of a large bank in Richmond, Virginia.

Blacks are also willing to study and make progress in farming. The late Mr. Chamberliss is one example. After Mr. Chamberliss' death, he bequeathed most of his property to build a school and a kindergarten in Tuskegee to educate many colored children in the city, which is of no small benefit to his people.

The cooperative movement is gradually gaining influence among blacks, which is also very promising. Now, there are black store associations in various places, which reduce the burden of independence and improve the quality of goods to attract broader business. Blacks who open stores are mostly known for their kindness to customers. White stores in the new southern provinces also hire blacks as managers.

Some people are overly concerned that the increase in the number of blacks and the opening of their minds will intensify competition for jobs between blacks and whites, or even lead to major conflicts. I believe that there is no such danger in the upper classes, but in the lower classes, such as laborers, conflicts may be inevitable due to the pursuit of work, but they will not be very serious and can be ignored.

Incidents of white people mistreating black people have gradually decreased in recent years. According to the Tuskegee survey report, there were only 10 such incidents in 1929, one less than in 1928 and seven less than in 1925. After the incidents occur, white public opinion also pays great attention to them, unlike in the past when they were indifferent.

The number of blacks who are pastors has gradually decreased in recent years. It is now estimated that there is one pastor for every 534 blacks, while there is one pastor for every 983 whites. However, there are few who join churches, and the number of those seeking a Bachelor of Theology degree in schools has also decreased. However, blacks are more calm emotionally and more intellectually advanced.

Impressions of the People's Art Exhibition 203

Art should be popularized, and life should be artistic. These are two very popular sayings, and also something everyone hopes can be realized. Using the power of the people to promote art ensures that art will endure. Using the spirit of art to transform life prevents it from becoming dull. Recently, most people have felt a sense of unease in their lives, especially the people in the city, who show signs of distress everywhere. The decline of careers and the corruption of character are secondary. If we want to improve life and promote civil spirit, advocating noble fine arts and developing mass art are, of course, essential remedies. We understand the unprecedented Shanghai Special Municipality People's Art Exhibition in this way.

In Shanghai, a big city, if you want to find a place that is the most popular and accessible to the people, the City God Temple is definitely one of the best. Starting with the plaque that protects the corner of the sea, it encompasses everything. Every day, thousands of men, women, old, and young, come to worship this sacred place. Originally, the scenery of Yu Garden, the Huxinting Teahouse, the Zigzag Bridge, the Cuixiu Hall, and the Jade Exquisite Stone were already good. In addition, there are tea houses, antique shops, bird shops, second-hand book stalls... all kinds of embellishments, making the unique atmosphere even stronger. This first-ever People's Art Exhibition is held in the inner garden of the City God Temple, which is probably a perfect match.

On the opening day of the People's Art Exhibition, it drizzled and rained incessantly. The calligraphy and paintings hung in the hall and corridors trembled listlessly in the breeze. The scroll rods lightly tapped against the walls, making a crisp and monotonous sound. The visitors walked back and forth between the calligraphy and paintings with their hands behind their backs, as if standing on both sides were many tall and lean calligraphers and painters bowing to each other. On a rainy day, in this gloomy and silent hall and corridors, the impression of seeing Chinese calligraphy and paintings with a distant artistic conception seems to be very bleak.

The next day, the number of visitors increased by about two times, totaling around one thousand eight hundred. The entire garden suddenly became very lively. Entering through the main gate, you first had to sign your name. Because everyone was rushing ahead, there was some disorder. Walking into the passage, you could see many Chinese paintings on both walls. Some people brought packages and sundries and had to deposit them at the cloakroom before entering the main hall to see the paintings. In the main hall, vertical scrolls, screen panels, and small paintings created an extraordinary realm. Several elderly viewers carefully looked from one painting to another, stroking their beards from time to time, nodding their heads up and down, and muttering to themselves. As for the general audience, they just slowed down their pace, passed through the hall and corridor, and then climbed up the artificial mountain. There were many children in the venue, like butterflies among flowers, running from east to west, happy and laughing.

Calligraphy couplets and the like were displayed in Qingxue Hall, with all styles of regular script, cursive script, clerical script, and seal script. The visitors seemed to have less interest in this section. Not only did the children not even glance at it, but even the gentlemen with long sleeves became relatively calm and serious in their expressions as soon as they entered Qingxue Hall, and their pace quickened. Therefore, it was not easy to see many people standing together in this room. Even if someone was looking at the wall, it was just like the prodigy in the book reading ten lines at a glance. After seeing the calligraphy, they went up to Yanqing Tower to see Western paintings and photography.

Before going up to Yanqing Tower, you had to pass through Songcui Pavilion, where many photographic works were displayed. The works were indeed very good, but there were fewer people crowding to see them than in front of the photography studio on the street. Most of the Western paintings were oil paintings. There were indeed many exquisite works, but some were inevitably immature and stiff. There were also several nude oil paintings. Several young sightseers, with their arms around each other's necks, lingered in front of a larger nude woman for a while, muttered something incomprehensible, and then left together. The Western painting exhibition hall was not very spacious, but the exhibits were very enthusiastic. The walls were full of brightly colored frames, arranged so tightly that no water could escape. At first glance when running up to Yanqing Tower, it was like running into a hardware store specializing in picture frames. The opportunity to appreciate the paintings seemed to be mostly occupied by the picture frames.

The inner garden is not easily opened at ordinary times. This time, due to the opportunity of the People's Exhibition, there were not a few who were able to admire the famous garden. If it could be permanently opened, it would not necessarily be a good thing for the people. However, the following section cannot be taken lightly.

An office worker said to the old gentleman in charge of the garden, "That white pomegranate tree next to the artificial mountain is very rare and precious. We should pay attention and not let the children climb and break it." The old gentleman was already old. After hearing this, he sighed slightly, but said excitedly, "That's why it can't be opened. Once it's open, I don't know how it will be ruined." After the old gentleman said this, he was silent, lowered his head, and took furious puffs on his dry tobacco pipe, as if the ten-day exhibition period was very long.

The Story of World Literature (169) by John Macy, Translated by Hu Zhongchi 204

Chapter 43: Italian Literature After the Renaissance

In poetry, the pioneer of the new era, the most important figure in the sincere Italian dramatic literature of the eighteenth century, is Alfieri, who possesses both first-class dramatic power and a sincere style. His main materials are mostly classical, such as Greek legends and ancient history. However, the style, although somewhat based on Machiavelli, is fresh and vigorous, Alfieri's own. Alfieri's plays have never crossed the border into English literature, yet he is important as a playwright, poet, and prose writer. We should know his ode praising American independence (he was a passionate admirer of freedom and an enemy of tyrants). As far as I know, this has never been translated into English.

The most magnificent Italian author of the eighteenth century is Parini. His "Day" (Il Giorno) is a sharp satire. By means of the fresh use of that heroic blank verse, Parini deservedly earned the title of "Modern Italian Virgil" bestowed by Leopardi on the older poet. Although Parini had a love for the classical past, he was an independent and original figure. A less original but more subservient figure, but also with excellent talent, is Monti. His importance is largely due to the fact that he explains the relationship between literature and practical problems. He wrote poems praising Napoleon that were somewhat flattering, but his right to demand a high position in literature lies in his translation of the Iliad, which is ultimately recognized as the best Italian translation.

Together with Ugo Foscolo, we enter the nineteenth century both in time and in spirit. The publication of "The Last Letters of Jacopo Ortis" two years before the birth of the new century made him the Italian Goethe, although far narrower in scope than the great German. The suffering of Italy under the dual shackles of Austria and her accomplice Napoleon is reflected in this book. One might think that the literary relationship between Italy and England, two countries almost at opposite ends of Europe, is the most interesting example to be explained by Foscolo. A major essay on this relationship remains to be written. Many English poets have lived and died in Italy. At least Rossetti, an excellent English poet, is of pure Italian descent. Foscolo lived in England for many years and was a recognized and respected figure in the English critical arena. His poetry, although narrow in scope, is beautiful. His "Poems on Sepulchres" are poignant lyrical poems. His direct relationship with English literature lies in his translation of Sterne's "Sentimental Journey."

Thus, we move on to Leopardi, the greatest Italian genius of the nineteenth century, regarded as a sad, desolate, and world-weary poet, but also a natural singer. We can roughly regard him as the Italian Byron. He is inferior to the Italian poet in terms of vigor and productivity, but superior in terms of delicacy and completion. His magic has not been transplanted into English, and probably cannot be transplanted. The English scholar Bickersteth has written an interesting and informative book about Leopardi. However, English poems composed "in the rhythm of the original" are thousands of miles away from the Italian. Translation in this area, if not strictly following the words, is the art of recreating in the translator's language. One must be one or the other. However, even for the sake of Dante and Leopardi, it may not be impossible to acquire the knowledge of Italian sufficient to read them. This is what I dare to advise.

In fiction, the Romantic spirit is best represented by Manzoni. Let's make another loose, uncritical, but suggestive comparison: he is the Italian Walter Scott. His novel "The Betrothed" (I Promessi Sposi) is a first-class novel. It has entered all the languages of Europe, and although not the masterpiece that Italians seem to believe, it is still a work that is enjoyed with relish. In it, there is a kind of enchanting tenderness, and the style that Manzoni spent many years painstakingly perfecting has been helpful in maintaining Italian prose on a healthy foundation when it is in danger of soaring into empty rhetoric. He was a man endowed with all kinds of genius. His tragedies are mainly famous and praised now because he wrote them. However, his first drama "Count Carmagnola," which is independent of tradition and novel in form, also caught the eye of Goethe, a philosopher so insightful that he often discovered beauty. Manzoni is a lyrical poet of overflowing brilliance.

Page 30

The poem he wrote when Napoleon died (Il Cinque Maggio) is known everywhere where Italian is used. In this simple literary story, at least the beautiful "Requiem" by Verdi, which is in memory of Manzoni, is worth recording, especially if we strive to discover the unity of the arts and the continuity of human expression.

Carducci, an Italian poet of the mid-nineteenth century, a poet who cannot be translated and have significant value, was both a poet and a critic, and compiled older Italian poets with skillful hands. He is a surprising example of a literary professor and artist. His poems are concise, rigorous, and profound. In terms of the depth of meaning and the completion of form, no modern Italian poet has surpassed him.

In fiction, modern Italy has several talented figures, but few of the first-class genius. The most outstanding is probably the Sicilian Verga. He is mainly known outside of Italy for his novel "Cavalleria Rusticana." That novel is the basis for Mascagni's very popular opera. However, Verga's work is greater than that romantic short story. It is a social and emotional history of Sicily and Southern Italy.

Regarding the existing Italians, we can only say a word or two. D'Annunzio is a poet, playwright, novelist, aviator, and politician. His versatility and energy are unbelievably like the most vigorous men of the Renaissance, no one surpassed him in strength. His wording is amazing. Probably no other Italian in any era has been the possessor of such a vast vocabulary. Perhaps there is a smell of charlatan and posturing in him, but his works have not only stirred his compatriots but have also shaken all of Europe. And certainly, the man who wrote "The Triumph of Death" and "The Flame of Life" belongs to the prince of unworthy men. His lyrical poems are full of eloquence and bordering on verbosity. His plays, although somewhat rhetorical, are tense and colorful. The story of Francesca da Rimini, which he wrote with Duse as the heroine, is the kind of sensational literature that does not often appear on modern or any stage.

Young Italians like Papini and Marinetti are trying bold experiments with new forms and revolutionary ideas. A magnificent writer of short stories, which is not revolutionary in structure but classically complete, is Giuseppe Enrico. One thing seems certain: tastes are changing, schools are shifting, but Italy, the land of violent romantic gestures, will remain largely faithful to its ancient ancestors and will remain a child of the classics.
